## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching

4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Domain Lineage: Kubernetes Watch Event Delivery Path

## Your Task

Trace how a Kubernetes watch event is generated and delivered from etcd to a client application. Find: 1. In `etcd-io/etcd`: the Go file that defines the `watchStream` or `serverWatchStream` that sends events from the etcd MVCC store. 2. In `kubernetes/kubernetes`: the Go files under `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/` that implement the watch cache and event distribution (look for `Cacher` and `watchCache`). 3. In the kubernetes client-go ecosystem: the Go file that defines the `Reflector` that receives watch events on the client side. Report the repo, file path, and struct/type name for each hop.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the domain domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
*(none — all repos available locally)*

61-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've successfully traced the Kubernetes watch event delivery path from etcd to client and created the comprehensive answer.json file. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Watch Event Delivery Chain

**1. etcd (Event Source)**
- **`server/mvcc/watcher.go`**: Defines `watchStream` struct that collects watchers and streams events from the MVCC store
- **`server/etcdserver/api/v3rpc/watch.go`**: Defines `serverWatchStream` struct that manages the gRPC stream interface to clients

**2. Kubernetes API Server (Event Cache & Distribution)**
- **`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/cacher.go`**: `Cacher` struct implements storage.Interface, with `Watch()` method creating watch streams (lines 515-693) and `dispatchEvents()` distributing events (lines 1033-1092)
- **`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/watch_cache.go`**: `watchCache` struct maintains a circular buffer of events with resource version tracking
- **`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/cache_watcher.go`**: `cacheWatcher` struct implements watch.Interface with input and result channels for individual client connections

**3. Kubernetes Client (Event Consumer)**
- **`tools/cache/reflector.go`**: `Reflector` struct's `ListAndWatch()` method initiates watches via `listerWatcher.Watch()` and processes events from the API server

**Event Flow**: 
```
etcd watchStream → serverWatchStream (gRPC) → Cacher → dispatchEvents() → 
cacheWatcher.ResultChan() → Reflector.ListAndWatch() → Store/Cache
```

The answer file is now ready at `/workspace/answer.json` with all required files, symbols, and a detailed narrative explanation of the event delivery path.

The watcher watches the events happening or\\n39: \\t// happened on the given key or range [key, end) from the given startRev.\\n40: \\t//\\n41: \\t// The whole event history can be watched unless compacted.\\n42: \\t// If \\\"startRev\\\" <=0, watch observes events after currentRev.\\n43: \\t//\\n44: \\t// The returned \\\"id\\\" is the ID of this watcher. The response\\n54: \\t// will only be sent if the watcher is currently synced.\\n55: \\t// The responses will be sent through the WatchRespone Chan attached\\n56: \\t// with this stream to ensure correct ordering.\\n57: \\t// The responses contains no events.
